###begin article-title 0
###xml 51 58 51 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 51 58 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Eukaryotic HMGB proteins as replacements for HU in E. coli repression loop formation
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 0 16 0 16 <!--CREATIVE COMMONS-->
CREATIVE COMMONSThis is an Open Access article distributed under the terms of the Creative Commons Attribution Non-Commercial License ( which permits unrestricted non-commercial use, distribution, and reproduction in any medium, provided the original work is properly cited.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 63 79 63 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 510 517 510 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 624 631 624 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 737 744 737 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 832 839 832 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 992 999 992 999 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 63 79 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 510 517 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 624 631 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 690 695 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 737 744 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 832 839 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1014 1019 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
DNA looping is important for gene repression and activation in Escherichia coli and is necessary for some kinds of gene regulation and recombination in eukaryotes. We are interested in sequence-nonspecific architectural DNA-binding proteins that alter the apparent flexibility of DNA by producing transient bends or kinks in DNA. The bacterial heat unstable (HU) and eukaryotic high-mobility group B (HMGB) proteins fall into this category. We have exploited a sensitive genetic assay of DNA looping in living E. coli cells to explore the extent to which HMGB proteins and derivatives can complement a DNA looping defect in E. coli lacking HU protein. Here, we show that derivatives of the yeast HMGB protein Nhp6A rescue DNA looping in E. coli lacking HU, in some cases facilitating looping to a greater extent than is observed in E. coli expressing normal levels of HU protein. Nhp6A-induced changes in the DNA length-dependence of repression efficiency suggest that Nhp6A alters DNA twist in vivo. In contrast, human HMGB2-box A derivatives did not rescue looping.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
INTRODUCTION
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 85 86 85 86 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 87 88 87 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 106 113 106 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 115 118 115 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3 B4 B5 B6">3&#8211;6</xref>
###xml 227 230 227 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B7 B8 B9">7&#8211;9</xref>
###xml 459 464 459 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10 B11 B12 B13">10&#8211;13</xref>
###xml 579 580 579 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 581 582 581 582 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 583 588 583 588 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14 B15 B16 B17 B18 B19 B20 B21">14&#8211;21</xref>
The intrinsic stiffness of double-stranded DNA with respect to bending and twisting (1,2) must be managed in vivo (3-6). This is particularly true because of the need to compact very long genomes into the prokaryotic nucleoid (7-9) or eukaryotic nucleus. Enhancing the apparent flexibility of DNA is apparently also essential to facilitate locally deformed nucleoprotein structures such as loops, required for certain kinds of gene control and recombination (10-13). Architectural DNA-binding proteins appear to play important roles in modifying the apparent flexibility of DNA (5,6,14-21).
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 43 59 43 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 240 245 240 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22 B23 B24 B25 B26 B27 B28 B29">22&#8211;29</xref>
###xml 347 358 347 358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli gal</italic>
###xml 367 369 367 369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 370 372 370 372 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 618 621 618 621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lac</italic>
###xml 649 651 649 651 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 652 654 652 654 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 671 674 671 674 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lac</italic>
###xml 810 817 810 817 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 819 821 819 821 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 822 824 822 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 825 827 825 827 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 43 59 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 347 354 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 810 817 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The abundant heat unstable (HU) protein of Escherichia coli binds DNA with little or no sequence specificity, and induces a sharp DNA bend. X-ray crystallography and biochemical experiments suggest HU can induce hinge-like DNA flexibility (22-29). This protein appears to play a direct role in facilitating DNA loop formation in repression of the E. coli gal operon (30,31). In this case, an A/T-rich sequence element may be the preferred HU-binding site in the DNA loop, and direct GalR-HU interactions have been proposed. Though HU had not been previously implicated in facilitating repression by DNA looping in the lac operon, our previous work (14,15) has shown that lac repression becomes leaky in the absence of HU. Deletion of the genes encoding HU results in nucleoid instability and growth defects in E. coli (24,32,33).
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 165 166 165 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 167 169 167 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 310 318 294 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 328 333 312 317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35 B36 B37 B38 B39 B40 B41 B42 B43">35&#8211;43</xref>

###xml 674 676 652 654 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 983 985 937 939 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 1319 1321 1237 1239 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 1373 1374 1291 1292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 1374 1375 1292 1293 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</sub>
###xml 1675 1677 1563 1565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 1774 1776 1662 1664 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 1978 1987 1860 1869 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 1.</label>
###xml 2006 2021 1888 1903 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli in vivo</italic>
###xml 2042 2043 1924 1925 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>

###xml 2663 2665 2541 2543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 2666 2668 2544 2546 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 2754 2767 2632 2645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 2775 2777 2653 2655 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 3096 3097 2974 2975 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
###xml 3166 3168 3044 3046 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 3169 3171 3047 3049 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 3181 3182 3059 3060 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 3197 3200 3075 3078 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 3275 3282 3153 3160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 3312 3316 3190 3194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 3674 3681 3549 3556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1987 3836 1869 3707 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="7">Proteins tested in <italic>E. coli in vivo</italic> DNA-looping assay. (<bold>A</bold>) HMGB proteins tested. The plasmid number and a description of protein domains (amino-to-carboxyl order) are indicated, along with the complete amino acid sequence aligned at conserved HMG box intercalating residues (vertical bars). The c-Myc epitope tag is indicated by &#8216;X&#8217; and its sequence is given below the figure. Deletion derivatives removed portions of cationic tails at the amino (constructs 1299, 1328) or carboxyl (construct 1493) termini. The &#945;-helical domains I, II and III are indicated below the diagram. (<bold>B</bold>) Molecular models of single HMG boxes bound to DNA. Left, HMG box A from mammalian HMGB1 (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>,<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>,<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>), PDB code 1CKT, which is highly similar to the corresponding box from HMGB2. Right, <italic>S. cerevisiae</italic> Nhp6A (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>), pdb code 1J5N. The strongly bent DNA molecules are shown as space-filling models in cyan. HMGB domains are shown in red. Note that both the amino and carboxyl termini (N and C, respectively) are positioned so that basic tail extensions can neutralize crowded DNA backbone phosphates in the compressed major groove. (<bold>C</bold>) Schematic representation of episomal lac looping assay constructs (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>,<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>). Weak (O<sub>2</sub>) and strong (O<sub>sym</sub>) lac operators are positioned at various separation distances flanking an <italic>E. coli</italic> promoter (P) upstream of the <italic>lacZ</italic> reporter gene encoding &#946;-galactosidase. In the presence of tetrameric lac repressor protein, DNA looping causes repression of the test promoter. The dependence of DNA looping on operator separation in a series of strains where this distance is varied in base pair increments provides information about the apparent bending and torsional stiffness of DNA <italic>in vivo</italic>. When experiments are performed in &#916;HU cells, the effect of apparent DNA flexibility of exogenous eukaryotic HMGB protein expression can be monitored.</p>

###xml 439 444 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 879 884 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 964 969 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1662 1667 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 2006 2013 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 2754 2767 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 3275 3282 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
In eukaryotes the abundant sequence-nonspecific high-mobility group B (HMGB) proteins appear to perform roles analogous to HU in enhancing apparent DNA flexibility (6,34). HMGB proteins contain one or two approximately80-amino acid domains that fold into 'L'-shaped structures composed of three alpha-helices [Figure 1A and B; (35-43)]. In the case of sequence-nonspecific DNA binding by HMGB proteins such as mammalian HMGB1 and HMGB2 or yeast Nhp6A, DNA bending of 90degrees or more results from van der Waals and electrostatic interactions of the globular domains with the minor groove and also amino acid intercalation to force local kinking (44). Recent studies (40,44,45) have estimated that an individual HMG box (B) from HMGB1 binds DNA with an equilibrium dissociation constant of approximately10 nM and a 40degrees induced bend angle. The single-box Nhp6A protein from yeast has been estimated to bend DNA by 60-90degrees. Our optical tweezer studies of human HMGB2 box A (16) showed that the protein reduced the apparent persistence length of DNA from its intrinsic value of 50 nm (approximately150 bp) to 10 nm (approximately30 bp) at 100 mM salt and even to 5 nm (approximately15 bp) at 50 mM salt. At saturation, protein binding increased the DNA contour length by 16% due to intercalation and unwinding (16). A binding site size of 5-6 bp was estimated with Kd approximately50-100 nM depending on the salt concentration. Average DNA bend angles of 114degrees and 87degrees were measured at 50 and 100 mM monovalent salt, respectively. More recent work using similar methods estimated DNA bending of 99degrees for the single HMG box A derived from human HMGB2 (17). Interestingly, a two-box HMGB protein may bind DNA with the protein domains out of alignment (42), and the NMR structure of such a protein bound to DNA gave an estimated DNA bend angle of 77degrees. Besides DNA bending, the degree of DNA untwisting by HMGB proteins depends on the protein variant. Figure 1.Proteins tested in E. coli in vivo DNA-looping assay. (A) HMGB proteins tested. The plasmid number and a description of protein domains (amino-to-carboxyl order) are indicated, along with the complete amino acid sequence aligned at conserved HMG box intercalating residues (vertical bars). The c-Myc epitope tag is indicated by 'X' and its sequence is given below the figure. Deletion derivatives removed portions of cationic tails at the amino (constructs 1299, 1328) or carboxyl (construct 1493) termini. The alpha-helical domains I, II and III are indicated below the diagram. (B) Molecular models of single HMG boxes bound to DNA. Left, HMG box A from mammalian HMGB1 (37,38,41), PDB code 1CKT, which is highly similar to the corresponding box from HMGB2. Right, S. cerevisiae Nhp6A (40), pdb code 1J5N. The strongly bent DNA molecules are shown as space-filling models in cyan. HMGB domains are shown in red. Note that both the amino and carboxyl termini (N and C, respectively) are positioned so that basic tail extensions can neutralize crowded DNA backbone phosphates in the compressed major groove. (C) Schematic representation of episomal lac looping assay constructs (14,15). Weak (O2) and strong (Osym) lac operators are positioned at various separation distances flanking an E. coli promoter (P) upstream of the lacZ reporter gene encoding beta-galactosidase. In the presence of tetrameric lac repressor protein, DNA looping causes repression of the test promoter. The dependence of DNA looping on operator separation in a series of strains where this distance is varied in base pair increments provides information about the apparent bending and torsional stiffness of DNA in vivo. When experiments are performed in DeltaHU cells, the effect of apparent DNA flexibility of exogenous eukaryotic HMGB protein expression can be monitored.Table 1.Bacterial strains in this studyStrainRelevant genotypeDesignationCommentFW102aStrepR derivative of CSH142 [araD(gpt-lac)5]WTBL643FW102 DeltahupA DeltahupBDeltaHULoss of both HU-1 and HU-2 subunits of HU heterodimeraFW102 was the kind gift of F. ###begin p 10
###xml 251 259 251 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 332 333 332 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 334 336 334 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 337 339 337 339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 340 342 340 342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B47">47</xref>
###xml 436 438 436 438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 607 609 595 597 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 891 898 879 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1136 1144 1124 1132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1146 1148 1134 1136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 891 898 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 950 955 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 992 997 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Of particular interest here are additional DNA-bending forces attributed to cationic tails at the amino or carboxy termini of HMGB proteins. Either terminus is positioned to interact with crowded phosphates in the compressed major groove of bent DNA (Figure 1B). These tails may enhance bending by asymmetric charge neutralization (2,44,46,47). An estimate of 4-5 degrees of DNA bending per major groove salt bridge has been suggested (44). Removal of six cationic residues from the cationic carboxy-terminal tail of the sequence-specific HMGB protein LEF1 reduced DNA bending from 117degrees to 88degrees (44). In this work, we test whether this potential change in DNA bending has functional consequences by asking whether the highly cationic tail domains are essential for HMGB function in a heterologous assay system where the protein facilitates DNA looping by lac repressor protein in E. coli, as described below. We compare derivatives of the yeast Nhp6A protein to charge variants of human HMGB2 box A. The latter domain was selected for comparison with our detailed examination of its properties in single molecule experiments in vitro (16). Future studies will extend these approaches to the more conserved and robust box B of mammalian HMGB1.
###end p 10

###xml 769 771 769 771 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 791 798 791 798 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 907 910 883 886 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;19</sup>
###xml 952 954 928 930 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 1040 1042 1016 1018 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 1043 1045 1019 1021 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 1102 1104 1078 1080 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 1177 1182 1153 1158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57 B58 B59">57&#8211;59</xref>
The in vivo lac repression looping assay (14,15,48-53) was developed to understand the constraints on DNA repression loops in living bacteria due to inflexibility in the repressor protein and looped DNA. As shown in Figure 1C, the lacZ reporter gene is placed downstream from a simple promoter that overlaps a very weak binding site (O2 operator) for lac repressor. This gene is poorly repressed. Repression is dramatically enhanced by placement of a strong operator (Osym) upstream of the promoter. Analysis of lacZ repression as a function of operator spacing provides an extremely sensitive assay of DNA bending and twisting flexibility in vivo (4,14,15,48,54,55). In particular, fitting the oscillating plots of the repression dependence on operator spacing (14,15,48) suggests that the in vivo apparent DNA torsional modulus is approximately4-fold lower than the accepted range of approximately2-4 x 10-19 erg cm for naked DNA in dilute solution (56). DNA bending stiffness did not appear to affect looping for loop sizes of 60-90 bp (14,15). Such short loops are highly unfavorable in naked DNA (19), though exactly how unfavorable has been the subject of recent debate (57-59).
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 30 37 30 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 119 126 119 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 174 176 174 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 177 179 177 179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 401 403 401 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 119 126 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
We have previously shown that in vivo lac repressor looping assays can be applied to understand the role of endogenous E. coli nucleoid proteins in facilitating DNA looping (14,15). In particular, cells disrupted for the genes encoding HU subunits were significantly disabled with respect to formation of repression loops, while cells lacking the H-NS nucleoid protein showed facilitated DNA looping (15). The detailed DNA length dependence of looping efficiency can be interpreted in terms of protein-induced changes in DNA structure or flexibility.
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 46 53 42 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 271 273 267 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 333 340 329 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 543 551 539 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 553 554 549 550 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B5">5</xref>
###xml 691 693 687 689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B60">60</xref>
###xml 763 770 755 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 889 891 881 883 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 46 53 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 305 310 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 333 340 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 596 601 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 684 689 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 763 770 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 822 825 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
The compromised repression looping in DeltaHU E. coli provides an opportunity to test the ability of heterologous eukaryotic HMGB proteins and mutants to complement this looping defect. Such complementation has been suggested by previous studies. Johnson and co-workers (18) showed that expression of the yeast HMGB protein Nhp6A in E. coli cells deleted for the HU and Fis nucleoid proteins restored normal nucleoid morphology and cell growth. Similarly, HMGB proteins substitute for bacterial HU in reconstituted DNA recombination reactions in vitro (5). It has also been shown that HU and the yeast mitochondrial HM protein can functionally replace each other in both bacteria and yeast (60). Our own initial studies of DNA looping by lac repressor in DeltaHU E. coli showed that heterologous expression of the two-box rat HMGB1 protein could partially restore facilitated DNA looping (14).
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 74 81 70 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 74 81 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 130 135 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 140 145 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
We now extend the study of HMGB complementation of DNA looping in DeltaHU E. coli by testing single box HMGB domains derived from yeast and human proteins. We further explore the importance of cationic HMGB tail domains by comparing complementation by constructs containing or lacking these extensions.
###end p 14
###begin title 15
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 15
###begin title 16
Bacterial strains and gene disruption
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 53 60 53 60 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 66 70 66 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hupA</italic>
###xml 75 79 75 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hupB</italic>
###xml 113 120 113 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 135 137 135 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 153 155 153 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 156 158 156 158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B62">62</xref>
###xml 113 120 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The bacterial strains in this study are indicated in Table 1. The hupA and hupB genes were disrupted in parental E. coli strain FW102 (61) as described (14,62). Strain deletion status and the presence of looping assay episomes were confirmed by diagnostic PCR amplification following conjugation and selection.
###end p 17

###xml 1189 1190 1189 1190 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1191 1192 1191 1192 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1194 1195 1194 1195 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1307 1308 1307 1308 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1310 1311 1310 1311 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1315 1316 1315 1316 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 1317 1318 1317 1318 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1322 1323 1322 1323 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1324 1325 1324 1325 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1327 1328 1327 1328 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>

###xml 1365 1366 1365 1366 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1380 1381 1380 1381 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1383 1384 1383 1384 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1388 1389 1388 1389 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1391 1392 1391 1392 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1394 1395 1394 1395 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sub>
###xml 1397 1398 1397 1398 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1373 1399 1373 1399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CAGATCT<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>2</sub>CAGA<sub>3</sub>TA<sub>2</sub>GT<sub>5</sub>GT<sub>2</sub>C</italic>
###xml 1373 1399 1373 1399 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>CAGATCT<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>2</sub>CAGA<sub>3</sub>TA<sub>2</sub>GT<sub>5</sub>GT<sub>2</sub>C</italic></bold>
###xml 1402 1403 1402 1403 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1404 1405 1404 1405 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1408 1409 1408 1409 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1412 1413 1412 1413 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1418 1419 1418 1419 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1456 1459 1456 1459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xba</italic>
###xml 1536 1539 1536 1539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Hin</italic>
###xml 1649 1650 1649 1650 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1655 1656 1655 1656 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1658 1659 1658 1659 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1661 1662 1661 1662 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1663 1664 1663 1664 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1666 1667 1666 1667 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1668 1669 1668 1669 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 603 608 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
HMG protein expression constructs were created by inserting purified PCR products into plasmid pJ1035, which is a modified version of pLX20 containing a promoter for a moderate level of protein expression and an inactive lac operator (14,61). Both full length (pJ1200 and pJ1327) and deletion (pJ1299 and pJ1328) versions of Nhp6A were created for protein expression. In addition, a 10-amino acid c-Myc epitope tag (EQKLISEEDL) was added either to the N-terminus (pJ1200 and pJ1299), or the C-terminus (pJ1327 and pJ1328) of proteins to monitor expression. Nhp6A constructs were amplified from purified yeast genomic DNA. Briefly, pJ1200 contains the product of PCR with primer pair LJM-2498 (GCTCTAGA2TGGA2CA5CT2AT3CTGA3GA3GATCTGGTCAC4A2GAGA2C2TA2G) and LJM-2473 (CGAC2G2TCGCAGTC3TA2GC2A3GTG2CG), which amplify the coding region of Nhp6A from Met1 to Ala92. The encoded c-Myc tag is indicated in bold italics. Upper primer LJM-2498 also installs an XbaI site and lower primer LJM-2473 installs both a stop codon and an AgeI site for cloning. Nhp6A deletion construct pJ1299, missing amino acids 2-12, was created using upper primer LJM-2564 (GCTCTAGA2TG2A2CA5CT2AT3CTGA2GA2GATCTGAGA3GA2GA2G2AC3) and lower primer LJM-2473. Full length Nhp6A construct pJ1327 was created using primer pair LJM-2701 (GCTCTAGA2TG2TCAC4A2GAGA2C2TA2G) and lower primer LJM-2704 (CGA2GCT2GCAGCTACAGATCT2CT2CAGA3TA2GT5GT2CAGC2A3GTG2CGT2ATATA2C). Upper primer LJM-2701 installs a XbaI site. Lower primer LJM-2704 installs the c-Myc tag, a TAG stop codon and a Hind III restriction site for cloning. Deletion construct pJ1328 was created with upper primer LJM-2702 (GCTCTAGA2TGAGA3GA2GA2G2AC3A3TG) and lower primer LJM-2704.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 305 306 305 306 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 310 311 310 311 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 313 314 313 314 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sub>
###xml 316 317 316 317 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 319 320 319 320 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 324 325 324 325 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 327 328 327 328 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 308 334 308 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GA<sub>2</sub>CA<sub>5</sub>CT<sub>2</sub>AT<sub>3</sub>CTGA<sub>2</sub>GA<sub>2</sub>GATCTG</italic>
###xml 308 334 308 334 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><italic>GA<sub>2</sub>CA<sub>5</sub>CT<sub>2</sub>AT<sub>3</sub>CTGA<sub>2</sub>GA<sub>2</sub>GATCTG</italic></bold>
###xml 335 336 335 336 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 338 339 338 339 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>

###xml 345 346 345 346 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 347 348 347 348 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 418 419 418 419 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 422 423 422 423 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 432 433 432 433 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 435 436 435 436 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 437 438 437 438 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sub>
###xml 440 441 440 441 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 594 595 594 595 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 598 599 598 599 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>

###xml 612 613 612 613 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 615 616 615 616 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 617 618 617 618 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 622 623 622 623 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 624 625 624 625 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">5</sub>
###xml 37 42 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 463 468 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Plasmid constructs encoding box A of human HMGB2 were amplified from plasmid pJ583 (a gift from Phillip Sharp), with the addition of N-terminal c-Myc tags. A variant construct deletes the basic linker region (amino acids 84-92: DKKGKKKDP). Plasmid pJ1492 was prepared using upper primer LJM-3315 (GCTCTAGA2TGGA2CA5CT2AT3CTGA2GA2GATCTGG2TA3G2AGAC4A2C), with the c-Myc tag in bold italics, and lower primer LJM-3317 (CGA2GCT2GCAGCTACG3TC2T5CT2C), which amplify the human HMGB2 coding region from Met1 to Pro92. Plasmid pJ1493 was created using upper primer LJM-3315 and lower primer LJM-3327 (CGA2GCT2GCAGCTA2C2T3G3AG2A2CGTA2T5C), which amplify from Met1 to Gly83 of HMGB2A.
###end p 20
###begin title 21
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">In vivo</italic>
In vivo DNA-looping assay
###end title 21
###begin p 22
###xml 92 94 92 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 121 123 121 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 164 167 164 167 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 198 199 198 199 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 215 216 215 216 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 254 258 254 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 317 319 317 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 351 352 351 352 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 375 378 375 378 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 479 483 479 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 648 652 648 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacI</italic>
###xml 720 724 720 724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacI</italic>
###xml 933 935 933 935 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
DNA-looping constructs were based on plasmid pJ992, created by modifications of pFW11-null (61) as previously described (14). Constructs contained a strong distal Osym operator and a weak proximal O2 operator. The O2 operator normally present within the lacZ coding region was destroyed by site-directed mutagenesis (14). A construct with a proximal O2 but lacking upstream Osym was used as a normalization control. Test promoters did not contain promoter CAP-binding sites. The lacZ looping constructs were placed on the single copy F128 episome by homologous recombination between the constructed plasmids and bacterial episome. F128 carries the lacI gene producing wild-type levels of repressor. Maintaining both the lacI gene and the target promoter in single copy ensures that the protein and DNA concentrations are as close to wild-type as possible. Bacterial conjugation and selections were performed as previously described (61). After mating and selection, correct recombinants were confirmed by PCR amplification.
###end p 22
###begin title 23
Reporter assay
###end title 23
###begin p 24
###xml 64 68 64 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 164 166 161 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B63">63</xref>
###xml 570 573 551 554 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">600</sub>
###xml 755 756 720 721 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 759 760 724 725 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 771 772 736 737 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 774 775 739 740 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 805 806 770 771 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 1248 1249 1196 1197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">O</italic>
###xml 1363 1366 1305 1308 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">420</sub>
###xml 1435 1436 1364 1365 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1438 1439 1367 1368 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 1556 1557 1485 1486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 1762 1763 1687 1688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 1843 1844 1768 1769 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x</sub>
###xml 1843 1844 1768 1769 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>x</sub></italic>
###xml 1885 1889 1810 1814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x, t</italic>
###xml 1922 1923 1847 1848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">v</italic>
All chemicals were obtained from Sigma (St Louis, MO, USA). The lacZ expression was measured by a liquid beta-galactosidase colorimetric enzyme assay as described (63). The assay was modified to increase efficiency. Cultures were grown in 1.1 ml LB/antibiotic in 96-well boxes (2 ml capacity per well) with shaking (250 r.p.m.) at 37degreesC. Fresh 1.1 ml aliquots of media were then inoculated with 30 mul of overnight culture in the presence or absence of 2 mM isopropyl beta-D-1-thiogalactopyranoside (IPTG). Subcultures were grown with shaking at 37degreesC until OD600 reached approximately0.3. For samples with low beta-galactosidase activity, 800 mul of bacterial culture was assayed after centrifugation and resuspension in 1 ml Z-buffer (60 mM Na2HPO4, 40 mM NaH2PO4, pH 7.0, 10 mM KCl, 1 mM MgSO4, 50 mM beta-mercaptoethanol). For samples with high levels of beta-galactosidase activity, 100 mul of bacterial culture was diluted with 900 mul of Z-buffer before analysis. Cells were lyzed by addition of 50 mul chloroform and 25 mul 0.1% sodium dodecyl sulfate (SDS), followed by repeated pipetting (10-12 times) with a 12-channel pipettor. Samples were equilibrated at 30degreesC for 5 min, followed by the addition of 200 mul of 4 mg/ml O-nitrophenylpyranogalactoside (ONPG) in Z-buffer. Incubation at 30degreesC continued with accurate timing until OD420 reached approximately0.5. Reactions were stopped with 500 mul 1 M Na2CO3 and the reaction time was recorded. Cell debris was pelleted by centrifugation of the 96-well box for 10 min at 4000g. A total of 350 mul of cleared samples were transferred to 96-well plates. Sample OD readings were measured on a Molecular Devices SpectraMax 340 microtiter plate reader. The beta-galactosidase activity (E, in Miller units) was calculated according to the following equation:  where ODx refers to optical density at wavelength x, t is the reaction time (min), and v is the assay culture volume (ml). Assays were performed with a total of six colonies from each independent strain repeated on 2 different days.
###end p 24

###xml 150 151 150 151 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 145 151 145 151 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">OsymO<sub>2</sub></sub>
###xml 246 249 243 246 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 255 256 252 253 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 274 275 271 272 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>

###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 87 89 87 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 90 92 90 92 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 144 146 144 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E&#8242;</italic>
###xml 151 153 151 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RR</italic>
###xml 245 246 245 246 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 336 337 336 337 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 366 367 366 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 367 372 367 372 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">bound</sub>
###xml 421 423 421 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 570 571 570 571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</italic>
###xml 572 579 572 579 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">optimal</sub>
###xml 621 624 621 624 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 626 627 626 627 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 705 706 705 706 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 706 709 706 709 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 784 785 784 785 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 785 788 785 788 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NSL</sub>
###xml 795 796 795 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 796 799 796 799 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NSL</sub>
###xml 829 832 829 832 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 864 865 864 865 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 943 946 943 946 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 981 982 981 982 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 997 998 997 998 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1036 1039 1036 1039 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 1237 1238 1237 1238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 1238 1241 1238 1241 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 1380 1381 1380 1381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1381 1384 1381 1384 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
An extended version of a previously described statistical weights/DNA mechanics model (14,15) was used for simultaneous fitting of experimental E' and RR data. The model describes the distribution of looped, singly bound and free states of the O2 operator under repressed and induced conditions. The experimentally derived fraction of O2 that is bound by repressor (fbound) is modeled as a function of DNA spacer length (sp) with six adjustable parameters. Three parameters describe properties mainly of the LacI:DNA complex: the optimal operator spacing in base pairs (spoptimal), the equilibrium constant for specific Osym-O2 loop formation when operators are perfectly phased (, replacing our previous Kmax as discussed below), and an equilibrium constant for nonspecific looping (KNSL). The KNSL term describes all forms of Osym-dependent enhanced binding to O2 other than the specific loop; for example, it could include looping between Osym and a pseudooperator overlapping O2, or enhanced O2 binding via sliding or hopping from Osym. Three fitting parameters describe mainly properties of the intervening DNA; the first two, as in our previous work, are the helical repeat (hr) and the apparent torsional modulus of the DNA loop (Capp). The qualitatively obvious length dependence of some of the data sets obtained here prompted us to add a third fitting parameter denoted Papp.
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 0 1 0 1 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1 4 1 4 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 113 115 113 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 212 213 212 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 383 385 375 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 524 525 516 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 526 527 518 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 527 530 519 522 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 531 533 523 525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 525 533 517 525 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;<italic>P</italic><sub>app</sub>/<italic>sp</italic></sup>
###xml 577 578 569 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 578 581 570 573 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 627 628 619 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 699 700 691 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 700 703 692 695 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 766 768 758 760 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 768 771 760 763 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">avg</sub>
###xml 811 812 803 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 812 815 804 807 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 834 836 826 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 841 844 833 836 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">avg</sub>
###xml 839 844 831 836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp<sub>avg</sub></italic>
###xml 877 878 869 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 878 881 870 873 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 962 963 954 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 963 966 955 958 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 1021 1022 1013 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1022 1025 1014 1017 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 1091 1093 1083 1085 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 1093 1096 1085 1088 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">avg</sub>
###xml 1161 1162 1153 1154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1162 1165 1154 1157 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 1192 1193 1184 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1193 1196 1185 1188 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 1225 1226 1217 1218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 1226 1229 1218 1221 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 1240 1247 1232 1239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Papp is an empirical parameter motivated by the expected decrease in DNA-bending free energy as operator spacing sp increases, as given by the expression below:  where we have absorbed the DNA persistence length P, the thermal energy RT, and the extent of bending (DeltaTheta) into a single constant; for simplicity, we make the doubtful assumption of constant loop geometry for all sp. We do not have an independent measurement of absolute bending free energy at any length, but the bending energy above will contribute an e-Papp/sp factor in the looping equilibrium constant Kmax. Therefore, the functional form of Equation (4) is combined with normalization of the length dependence by replacing Kmax in the fitting routines with the following expression:  where spavg is the mean spacing over the data set. Kmax, the value of  at sp = spavg can be compared directly to the Kmax obtained using our previous fitting routines. For the data sets here, values of Kmax determined as previously described without the use of Papp agree to within their estimated uncertainties with  evaluated at spavg. None of the interpretations given here depend on the values of Papp except those that concern Papp itself. The relationship of Papp to a true in vivo DNA persistence length is complicated because the amount of curvature in the loop probably changes with spacing.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 38 39 38 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 39 42 39 42 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 560 561 560 561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 561 564 561 564 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
A second important motivation for the Papp parameter is that none of the other physical processes that we modeled can reproduce the observed increase in repression with increasing length. We were concerned that the multiparameter fitting procedure might lead to marked inaccuracies in the other values if the routines changed them to try to fit the length dependence. The results showed that this was not a serious problem, apparently because variations in the other parameters are simply unable to model the observations (not shown). However, we retained the Papp parameter in part because of the interesting trends in its values, as discussed subsequently.
###end p 30
###begin title 31
Assay of protein expression
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 1042 1047 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Derivatives of HMGB protein expression plasmid pJ1035 were transformed into BL643 (DeltaHU) bacterial cells and grown on LB-Cb plates. Individual colonies were grown in 5 ml LB-Cb liquid cultures overnight at 37degreesC with aeration. Saturated overnight culture (1.5 ml) was pelleted by centrifugation, resuspended in 300 microl 2-(N-morpholino) ethanesulfonic acid (MES) buffer (50 mM MES, 50 mM Tris base, 3 mM SDS, 1 mM EDTA, pH 7.5) and cells were lyzed by sonication in bursts of 3 s. Samples were clarified by centrifugation and analyzed on 10% bis-Tris gels containing SDS by electrophoresis at 145 V for 45 min in 1x MES buffer. Protein was transferred to a nitrocellulose membrane using NuPAGE transfer buffer containing 20% methanol (30 V, 3 h, 4degreesC). The primary antibody for western blotting was specific for the c-Myc tag (op10T, CalBiochem, San Diego, CA, USA). Blots were blocked for 1 h in blocking buffer, incubated with primary antibody overnight at 4degreesC in blocking buffer and then incubated with secondary anti-mouse antibody at room temperature for 1 h. Imaging was performed with ECL Plus western blot detection (Amersham, Piscataway, NJ, USA).
###end p 32
###begin title 33
RESULTS AND DISCUSSION
###end title 33
###begin title 34
Experimental design
###end title 34
###begin p 35
###xml 191 198 187 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 392 400 388 396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 97 102 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 113 118 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 191 198 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 596 601 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1121 1126 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Our primary goals in this work were (i) to determine to what extent the eukaryotic HMGB proteins yeast Nhp6A and human HMGB2A can complement the repression looping defect observed in DeltaHU E. coli cells, and (ii) to determine the importance of cationic amino acid terminal sequences of the HMGB proteins to any observed complementation. The experimental HMGB protein sequences are shown in Figure 1A. They contain decameric c-Myc epitope tags at the N-terminus (constructs 1200, 1299, 1492 and 1493) or C-terminus (constructs 1327 and 1328) as indicated in the designations. The initial tagged yeast Nhp6A construct is denoted 1200, and in 1299 there is a deletion of 11 of the native N-terminal amino acids of 1200. This deletion removes three of seven cationic amino acids from the Nhp6A N-terminal leader, adjacent to an N-terminal myc epitope tag that is anionic. To determine if the tag and its electrostatic character were important, Nhp6A constructs 1327 and 1328 were prepared with a C-terminal myc tag, with 1328 bearing the 11 amino acid N-terminal deletion relative to 1327. Constructs 1492 and 1493 contain human HMGB2 box A sequences with an N-terminal myc tag. The 1493 denotes a protein with a truncation of nine C-terminal residues (removing +3 net charge).
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 140 148 140 148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 410 412 410 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
Both the Nhp6A and HMGB proteins have been shown to fold into L-shaped clusters of three helical domains with N- and C-terminal extensions (Figure 1B). In the case of Nhp6A, the cationic N-terminal extension appears to neutralize crowded phosphates in the compressed major groove of the bent DNA. Truncation of a similar segment from the sequence-specific LEF-1 HMGB protein significantly reduces DNA bending (44). The C-terminal extension of HMGB appears to be disposed to serve a similar charge neutralization function.
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 130 137 126 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 192 200 188 196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 286 287 282 283 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 302 305 298 301 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 437 440 433 436 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 604 611 600 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 130 137 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
The ability of HMGB proteins to enhance the apparent flexibility of DNA and complement the DNA looping defect observed in DeltaHU E. coli was assayed as in our previous work, as diagrammed in Figure 1C. Efficient repression by lac repressor tetramer requires DNA looping between weak (O2) and strong (Osym) operators that flank the promoter (P). Experimental measurement of the extent of DNA repression (compared to constructs where no Osym was present) was used to test the hypothesis that nonhomologous prokaryotic HU and eukaryotic HMGB proteins can increase the apparent flexibility of DNA similarly in vivo.
###end p 37
###begin title 38
###xml 46 53 46 53 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 46 53 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Expression of epitope-tagged HMGB proteins in E. coli
###end title 38

###xml 61 68 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 459 466 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 808 813 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1018 1025 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1107 1114 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
We measured the accumulation of HMGB deletion derivatives in E. coli using western blots. Surprisingly, preliminary experiments showed that any truncation of Nhp6A that removed amino acids of the RK3 sequence near the N-terminus, regardless of the presence or absence of an N-terminal myc epitope tag, completely eliminated protein accumulation. This result suggests that proper folding of Nhp6A requires these cationic residues. The western blot analysis of E. coli extracts in Figure 2 shows the relative levels of accumulation of those proteins that could be expressed and tested, normalized to constant total protein. The Nhp6A derivatives were expressed at comparable levels except that construct 1327 (Figure 2A, lane 3) accumulated to a much lower although clearly detectable level. The full box A of human HMGB2 and its C-terminal truncated derivative accumulated to high levels compared to Nhp6A construct 1328 (Figure 2B, compare lanes 2-3 with lane 1). (B) Proteins expressed at higher levels. Lanes 1-3 correspond to proteins 1328 [Nhp6ADelta(2-12)/myc; repeated from panel A for comparison], 1492 (myc/hHMGB2A) and 1493 [myc/hHMGB2ADelta(84-92)], respectively.
###end p 39

###begin title 41
Complementation of DeltaHU phenotype by HMGB2 proteins and truncation mutants
###end title 41
###begin p 42
###xml 45 49 45 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lacZ</italic>
###xml 53 60 53 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 96 98 96 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E&#8242;</italic>
###xml 154 157 154 157 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sym</sub>
###xml 205 214 205 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 219 220 219 220 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4</xref>
###xml 321 330 321 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 335 336 335 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4</xref>

###xml 1060 1067 1050 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 1196 1203 1183 1190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 1048 1783 1038 1759 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="43">DNA looping <italic>in vivo</italic>. Top row: the repression ratio (ratio of &#946;-galactosidase activity under inducing versus noninducing conditions) is shown for <italic>E. coli</italic> WT, &#916;HU and &#916;HU strains expressing heterologous HMGB proteins. WT behavior is indicated by a shaded line in the three columns to the right. Bottom row: &#946;-galactosidase activity normalized to controls lacking an upstream operator under inducing (upper curves: filled circles) or noninducing (lower curves: open circles) conditions. Error bars represent standard deviations based on replicate measurements. Curve fitting to the thermodynamic model is shown. Shading indicates uninduced and induced reporter expression from WT cells. Raw data are available at NAR Online.</p>

###xml 3573 3876 3325 3628 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="46"><sup>a</sup>Indicated errors are 95% confidence limits. The values and ranges for <italic>K</italic><sub>max</sub>, <italic>K</italic><sub>NSL</sub> and <italic>P</italic><sub>app</sub> are fit only to expression data E+IPTG and E &#8722; IPTG. The values and ranges for <italic>sp</italic><sub>optimal</sub>, <italic>C</italic><sub>app</sub>, and <italic>hr</italic> are fit to E+IPTG, E &#8722; IPTG and the repression ratio RR simultaneously, with <italic>K</italic><sub>max</sub>, <italic>K</italic><sub>NSL</sub>, and <italic>P</italic><sub>app</sub> held fixed.</p>
###xml 3573 3876 3325 3628 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="TF2"><p textid="46"><sup>a</sup>Indicated errors are 95% confidence limits. ###xml 3876 3877 3628 3629 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</sup>
###xml 4012 4014 3762 3764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sp</italic>
###xml 4014 4021 3764 3771 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">optimal</sub>
###xml 4033 4034 3783 3784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 4034 4037 3784 3787 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 4049 4051 3799 3801 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hr</italic>
###xml 4063 4064 3813 3814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 4064 4067 3814 3817 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">max</sub>
###xml 4079 4080 3829 3830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">K</italic>
###xml 4080 4083 3830 3833 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">NSL</sub>
###xml 4115 4116 3865 3866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 4116 4119 3866 3869 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 4136 4137 3886 3887 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</italic>
###xml 4137 4140 3887 3890 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">app</sub>
###xml 4206 4208 3956 3958 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">hr</italic>
###xml 3876 4238 3628 3988 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="47"><sup>b</sup>Parentheses indicate a large error estimate, making the parameter value unreliable. However, trends &#177;IPTG are robust: upon induction <italic>sp</italic><sub>optimal</sub> increases, <italic>C</italic><sub>app</sub> decreases, <italic>hr</italic> decreases, <italic>K</italic><sub>max</sub> decreases, <italic>K</italic><sub>NSL</sub> decreases or is negligible and <italic>P</italic><sub>app</sub> increases. When <italic>C</italic><sub>app</sub> is less than about 0.3, torsional oscillations are so small that <italic>hr</italic> cannot be estimated reliably.</p>
###xml 3876 4238 3628 3988 <fn xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="TF3"><p textid="47"><sup>b</sup>Parentheses indicate a large error estimate, making the parameter value unreliable. ###xml 53 60 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 374 381 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 1196 1203 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
We measured DNA loop-dependent repression of lacZ in E. coli as reporter activity (expressed as E', the activity normalized to controls with no upstream Osym operator) in the presence and absence of IPTG (Figures 3 and 4, bottom row). The ratio of induced to uninduced raw activities is reported as the repression ratio (Figures 3 and 4, top row). The results for wild-type E. coli (Figure 3, 'WT' column) are entirely consistent with our previous studies, showing oscillating repression dependent on operator spacing, even in the presence of IPTG, with the +/-IPTG oscillations slightly shifted in phase and helical repeat so that the repression ratio is not sinusoidal (14,15). Looping was observed to be substantially disabled in DeltaHU cells (Figure 3, DeltaHU column), as we have previously reported (14,15). The resulting strain shows leaky repression of the lacZ reporter. Fitting parameters from the thermodynamic model of loop-dependent gene repression are given in Table 2, reflecting behavior consistent with our earlier work. Figure 3.DNA looping in vivo. Top row: the repression ratio (ratio of beta-galactosidase activity under inducing versus noninducing conditions) is shown for E. coli WT, DeltaHU and DeltaHU strains expressing heterologous HMGB proteins. WT behavior is indicated by a shaded line in the three columns to the right. Bottom row: beta-galactosidase activity normalized to controls lacking an upstream operator under inducing (upper curves: filled circles) or noninducing (lower curves: open circles) conditions. Error bars represent standard deviations based on replicate measurements. Curve fitting to the thermodynamic model is shown. Shading indicates uninduced and induced reporter expression from WT cells. Raw data are available at NAR Online.Figure 4.DNA looping in vivo. The repression ratio and normalized activities are shown as in Figure 3 for additional tested strains. In columns three and four, light colored curves show DeltaHU behavior for comparison. Considering length dependence explicitly clearly improves the fitting to the +IPTG E ' data.
